291→\tapplyTimeVariables := collections.NewSetCmp[string]()\n   292→\tfor k, iv := range opts.SetVariables {\n   293→\t\t// If any input variables were declared as ephemeral and set to a\n   294→\t\t// non-null value then those variables must be provided again (possibly\n   295→\t\t// with _different_ non-null values) during the apply phase.\n   296→\t\tif vc, ok := config.Module.Variables[k]; ok && vc.Ephemeral {\n   297→\t\t\t// FIXME: We should actually do this based on the final value\n   298→\t\t\t// in the named values state, rather than the value as provided\n   299→\t\t\t// by the caller, so we can take into account the transforms\n   300→\t\t\t// done during variable evaluation. This is a plausible starting\n   301→\t\t\t// point for now, though.\n   302→\t\t\tif iv.Value != cty.NilVal && !iv.Value.IsNull() {\n   303→\t\t\t\tapplyTimeVariables.Add(k)\n   304→\t\t\t}\n   305→\t\t\tcontinue\n   306→\t\t}\n   307→\n   308→\t\t// Non-ephemeral variables must remain unchanged between plan and\n   309→\t\t// apply, so we'll record their actual values.\n   310→\t\tif iv.Value == cty.NilVal {\n   311→\t\t\tcontinue // We only record values that the caller actually set\n   312→\t\t}\n   313→\n   314→\t\t// Root variable values arriving from the traditional CLI path are\n   315→\t\t// unmarked, as they are directly decoded from .tfvars, CLI arguments,\n   316→\t\t// or the environment. However, variable values arriving from other\n   317→\t\t// plans (via the coordination efforts of the stacks runtime) may have\n   318→\t\t// gathered marks during evaluation. We must separate the value from\n   319→\t\t// its marks here to maintain compatibility with plans.DynamicValue,\n   320→\t\t// which cannot represent marks.\n   321→\t\tvalue, pvm := iv.Value.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n   322→\n   323→\t\t// We use cty.DynamicPseudoType here so that we'll save both the\n   324→\t\t// value _and_ its dynamic type in the plan, so we can recover\n   325→\t\t// exactly the same value later.\n   326→\t\tdv, err := plans.NewDynamicValue(value, cty.DynamicPseudoType)\n   327→\t\tif err != nil {\n   328→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n   329→\t\t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n   330→\t\t\t\t\"Failed to prepare variable value for plan\",\n   331→\t\t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\"The value for variable %q could not be serialized to store in the plan: %s.\", k, err),\n   332→\t\t\t))\n   333→\t\t\tcontinue\n   334→\t\t}\n   335→\t\tvarVals[k] = dv\n   336→\t\tvarMarks[k] = pvm\n   337→\t}\n   338→\n   339→\t// insert the run-specific data from the context into the plan; variables,\n   340→\t// targets and provider SHAs.\n   341→\tif plan != nil {\n   342→\t\tplan.VariableValues = varVals\n   343→\t\tplan.ApplyTimeVariables = applyTimeVariables\n   344→\t\tif len(varMarks) > 0 {\n   345→\t\t\tplan.VariableMarks = varMarks\n   346→\t\t}\n   347→\t\tplan.TargetAddrs = opts.Targets\n   348→\t} else if !diags.HasErrors() {\n   349→\t\tpanic(\"nil plan but no errors\")\n   350→\t}\n   351→\n   352→\tif plan != nil {\n   353→\t\trelevantAttrs, rDiags := c.relevantResourceAttrsForPlan(config, plan)\n   354→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(rDiags)\n   355→\t\tplan.RelevantAttributes = relevantAttrs\n   356→\t}\n   357→\n   358→\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n   359→\t\t// We can't proceed further with an invalid plan, because an invalid\n   360→\t\t// plan isn't applyable by definition.\n   361→\t\tif plan != nil {\n   362→\t\t\t// We'll explicitly mark our plan as errored so that it can't\n   363→\t\t\t// be accidentally applied even though it's incomplete.\n   364→\t\t\tplan.Errored = true\n   365→\t\t}\n   366→\t\treturn plan, evalScope, diags\n   367→\t}\n   368→\n   369→\tdiags = diags.Append(c.checkApplyGraph(plan, config, opts))\n   370→\n   371→\treturn plan, evalScope, diags\n   372→}\n   373→\n   374→// checkApplyGraph builds the apply graph out of the current plan to\n   375→// check for any errors that may arise once the planned changes are added to\n   376→// the graph. This allows terraform to report errors (mostly cycles) during\n   377→// plan that would otherwise only crop up during apply\n   378→func (c *Context) checkApplyGraph(plan *plans.Plan, config *configs.Config, opts *PlanOpts) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n   379→\tif plan.Changes.Empty() {\n   380→\t\tlog.Println(\"[DEBUG] no planned changes, skipping apply graph check\")\n   381→\t\treturn nil\n   382→\t}\n   383→\tlog.Println(\"[DEBUG] building apply graph to check for errors\")\n   384→\n   385→\t_, _, diags := c.applyGraph(plan, config, opts.ApplyOpts(), true)\n   386→\treturn diags\n   387→}\n   388→\n   389→var DefaultPlanOpts = &PlanOpts{\n   390→\tMode: plans.NormalMode,\n   391→}\n   392→\n   393→// SimplePlanOpts is a constructor to help with creating \"simple\" values of\n   394→// PlanOpts which only specify a mode and input variables.\n   395→//\n   396→// This helper function is primarily intended for use in straightforward\n   397→// tests that don't need any of the more \"esoteric\" planning options. For\n   398→// handling real user requests to run Terraform, it'd probably be better\n   399→// to construct a *PlanOpts value directly and provide a way for the user\n   400→// to set values for all of its fields.\n   401→//\n   402→// The \"mode\" and \"setVariables\" arguments become the values of the \"Mode\"\n   403→// and \"SetVariables\" fields in the result. Refer to the PlanOpts type\n   404→// documentation to learn about the meanings of those fields.\n   405→func SimplePlanOpts(mode plans.Mode, setVariables InputValues) *PlanOpts {\n   406→\treturn &PlanOpts{\n   407→\t\tMode:         mode,\n   408→\t\tSetVariables: setVariables,\n   409→\t}\n   410→}\n   411→\n   412→func (c *Context) plan(config *configs.Config, prevRunState *states.State, opts *PlanOpts) (*plans.Plan, *lang.Scope, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   413→\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n   414→\tif opts.Mode != plans.NormalMode {\n   415→\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"called Context.plan with %s\", opts.Mode))\n   416→\t}\n   417→\n   418→\tplan, evalScope, walkDiags := c.planWalk(config, prevRunState, opts)\n   419→\tdiags = diags.Append(walkDiags)\n   420→\n   421→\treturn plan, evalScope, diags\n   422→}\n   423→\n   424→func (c *Context) refreshOnlyPlan(config *configs.Config, prevRunState *states.State, opts *PlanOpts) (*plans.Plan, *lang.Scope, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   425→\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n   426→\n   427→\tif opts.Mode != plans.RefreshOnlyMode {\n   428→\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"called Context.refreshOnlyPlan with %s\", opts.Mode))\n   429→\t}\n   430→\n   431→\tplan, evalScope, walkDiags := c.planWalk(config, prevRunState, opts)\n   432→\tdiags = diags.Append(walkDiags)\n   433→\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n   434→\t\t// Non-nil plan along with errors indicates a non-applyable partial\n   435→\t\t// plan that's only suitable to be shown to the user as extra context\n   436→\t\t// to help understand the errors.\n   437→\t\treturn plan, evalScope, diags\n   438→\t}\n   439→\n   440→\t// If the graph builder and graph nodes correctly obeyed our directive\n   441→\t// to refresh only, the set of resource changes should always be empty.\n   442→\t// We'll safety-check that here so we can return a clear message about it,\n   443→\t// rather than probably just generating confusing output at the UI layer.\n   444→\tif len(plan.Changes.Resources) != 0 {\n   445→\t\t// Some extra context in the logs in case the user reports this message\n   446→\t\t// as a bug, as a starting point for debugging.\n   447→\t\tfor _, rc := range plan.Changes.Resources {\n   448→\t\t\tif depKey := rc.DeposedKey; depKey == states.NotDeposed {\n   449→\t\t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[DEBUG] Refresh-only plan includes %s change for %s\", rc.Action, rc.Addr)\n   450→\t\t\t} else {\n   451→\t\t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[DEBUG] Refresh-only plan includes %s change for %s deposed object %s\", rc.Action, rc.Addr, depKey)\n   452→\t\t\t}\n   453→\t\t}\n   454→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n   455→\t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n   456→\t\t\t\"Invalid refresh-only plan\",\n   457→\t\t\t\"Terraform generated planned resource changes in a refresh-only plan. This is a bug in Terraform.\",\n   458→\t\t))\n   459→\t}\n   460→\n   461→\t// We don't populate RelevantResources for a refresh-only plan, because\n   462→\t// they never have any planned actions and so no resource can ever be\n   463→\t// \"relevant\" per the intended meaning of that field.\n   464→\n   465→\treturn plan, evalScope, diags\n   466→}\n   467→\n   468→func (c *Context) destroyPlan(config *configs.Config, prevRunState *states.State, opts *PlanOpts) (*plans.Plan, *lang.Scope, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   469→\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n   470→\n   471→\tif opts.Mode != plans.DestroyMode {\n   472→\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"called Context.destroyPlan with %s\", opts.Mode))\n   473→\t}\n   474→\n   475→\tpriorState := prevRunState\n   476→\n   477→\t// A destroy plan starts by running Refresh to read any pending data\n   478→\t// sources, and remove missing managed resources. This is required because\n   479→\t// a \"destroy plan\" is only creating delete changes, and is essentially a\n   480→\t// local operation.\n   481→\t//\n   482→\t// NOTE: if skipRefresh _is_ set then we'll rely on the destroy-plan walk\n   483→\t// below to upgrade the prevRunState and priorState both to the latest\n   484→\t// resource type schemas, so NodePlanDestroyableResourceInstance.Execute\n   485→\t// must coordinate with this by taking that action only when c.skipRefresh\n   486→\t// _is_ set. This coupling between the two is unfortunate but necessary\n   487→\t// to work within our current structure.\n   488→\tif !opts.SkipRefresh && !prevRunState.Empty() {\n   489→\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] Context.destroyPlan: calling Context.plan to get the effect of refreshing the prior state\")\n   490→\t\trefreshOpts := *opts\n   491→\t\trefreshOpts.Mode = plans.NormalMode\n   492→\t\trefreshOpts.PreDestroyRefresh = true\n   493→\n   494→\t\t// FIXME: A normal plan is required here to refresh the state, because\n   495→\t\t// the state and configuration may not match during a destroy, and a\n   496→\t\t// normal refresh plan can fail with evaluation errors. In the future\n   497→\t\t// the destroy plan should take care of refreshing instances itself,\n   498→\t\t// where the special cases of evaluation and skipping condition checks\n   499→\t\t// can be done.\n   500→\t\trefreshPlan, _, refreshDiags := c.plan(config, prevRunState, &refreshOpts)\n   501→\t\tif refreshDiags.HasErrors() {\n   502→\t\t\t// NOTE: Normally we'd append diagnostics regardless of whether\n   503→\t\t\t// there are errors, just in case there are warnings we'd want to\n   504→\t\t\t// preserve, but we're intentionally _not_ doing that here because\n   505→\t\t\t// if the first plan succeeded then we'll be running another plan\n   506→\t\t\t// in DestroyMode below, and we don't want to double-up any\n   507→\t\t\t// warnings that both plan walks would generate.\n   508→\t\t\t// (This does mean we won't show any warnings that would've been\n   509→\t\t\t// unique to only this walk, but we're assuming here that if the\n   510→\t\t\t// warnings aren't also applicable to a destroy plan then we'd\n   511→\t\t\t// rather not show them here, because this non-destroy plan for\n   512→\t\t\t// refreshing is largely an implementation detail.)\n   513→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(refreshDiags)\n   514→\t\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n   515→\t\t}\n   516→\n   517→\t\t// We'll use the refreshed state -- which is the  \"prior state\" from\n   518→\t\t// the perspective of this \"destroy plan\" -- as the starting state\n   519→\t\t// for our destroy-plan walk, so it can take into account if we\n   520→\t\t// detected during refreshing that anything was already deleted outside\n   521→\t\t// of Terraform.\n   522→\t\tpriorState = refreshPlan.PriorState.DeepCopy()\n   523→\n   524→\t\t// The refresh plan may have upgraded state for some resources, make\n   525→\t\t// sure we store the new version.\n   526→\t\tprevRunState = refreshPlan.PrevRunState.DeepCopy()\n   527→\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] Context.destroyPlan: now _really_ creating a destroy plan\")\n   528→\t}\n   529→\n   530→\tdestroyPlan, evalScope, walkDiags := c.planWalk(config, priorState, opts)\n   531→\tdiags = diags.Append(walkDiags)\n   532→\tif walkDiags.HasErrors() {\n   533→\t\t// Non-nil plan along with errors indicates a non-applyable partial\n   534→\t\t// plan that's only suitable to be shown to the user as extra context\n   535→\t\t// to help understand the errors.\n   536→\t\treturn destroyPlan, evalScope, diags\n   537→\t}\n   538→\n   539→\tif !opts.SkipRefresh {\n   540→\t\t// If we didn't skip refreshing then we want the previous run state to\n   541→\t\t// be the one we originally fed into the c.refreshOnlyPlan call above,\n   542→\t\t// not the refreshed version we used for the destroy planWalk.\n   543→\t\tdestroyPlan.PrevRunState = prevRunState\n   544→\t}\n   545→\n   546→\trelevantAttrs, rDiags := c.relevantResourceAttrsForPlan(config, destroyPlan)\n   547→\tdiags = diags.Append(rDiags)\n   548→\n   549→\tdestroyPlan.RelevantAttributes = relevantAttrs\n   550→\treturn destroyPlan, evalScope, diags\n   551→}\n   552→\n   553→func (c *Context) prePlanFindAndApplyMoves(config *configs.Config, prevRunState *states.State) ([]refactoring.MoveStatement, refactoring.MoveResults, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   554→\texplicitMoveStmts := refactoring.FindMoveStatements(config)\n   555→\timplicitMoveStmts := refactoring.ImpliedMoveStatements(config, prevRunState, explicitMoveStmts)\n   556→\tvar moveStmts []refactoring.MoveStatement\n   557→\tif stmtsLen := len(explicitMoveStmts) + len(implicitMoveStmts); stmtsLen > 0 {\n   558→\t\tmoveStmts = make([]refactoring.MoveStatement, 0, stmtsLen)\n   559→\t\tmoveStmts = append(moveStmts, explicitMoveStmts...)\n   560→\t\tmoveStmts = append(moveStmts, implicitMoveStmts...)\n   561→\t}\n   562→\tmoveResults, diags := refactoring.ApplyMoves(moveStmts, prevRunState, c.plugins.ProviderFactories())\n   563→\treturn moveStmts, moveResults, diags\n   564→}\n   565→\n   566→func (c *Context) prePlanVerifyTargetedMoves(moveResults refactoring.MoveResults, targets []addrs.Targetable) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n   567→\tif len(targets) < 1 {\n   568→\t\treturn nil // the following only matters when targeting\n   569→\t}\n   570→\n   571→\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n   572→\n   573→\tvar excluded []addrs.AbsResourceInstance\n   574→\tfor _, result := range moveResults.Changes.Values() {\n   575→\t\tfromMatchesTarget := false\n   576→\t\ttoMatchesTarget := false\n   577→\t\tfor _, targetAddr := range targets {\n   578→\t\t\tif targetAddr.TargetContains(result.From) {\n   579→\t\t\t\tfromMatchesTarget = true\n   580→\t\t\t}\n   581→\t\t\tif targetAddr.TargetContains(result.To) {\n   582→\t\t\t\ttoMatchesTarget = true\n   583→\t\t\t}\n   584→\t\t}\n   585→\t\tif !fromMatchesTarget {\n   586→\t\t\texcluded = append(excluded, result.From)\n   587→\t\t}\n   588→\t\tif !toMatchesTarget {\n   589→\t\t\texcluded = append(excluded, result.To)\n   590→\t\t}\n   591→\t}\n   592→\tif len(excluded) > 0 {\n   593→\t\tsort.Slice(excluded, func(i, j int) bool {\n   594→\t\t\treturn excluded[i].Less(excluded[j])\n   595→\t\t})\n   596→\n   597→\t\tvar listBuf strings.Builder\n   598→\t\tvar prevResourceAddr addrs.AbsResource\n   599→\t\tfor _, instAddr := range excluded {\n   600→\t\t\t// Targeting generally ends up selecting whole resources rather\n   601→\t\t\t// than individual instances, because we don't factor in\n   602→\t\t\t// individual instances until DynamicExpand, so we're going to\n   603→\t\t\t// always show whole resource addresses here, excluding any\n   604→\t\t\t// instance keys. (This also neatly avoids dealing with the\n   605→\t\t\t// different quoting styles required for string instance keys\n   606→\t\t\t// on different shells, which is handy.)\n   607→\t\t\t//\n   608→\t\t\t// To avoid showing duplicates when we have multiple instances\n   609→\t\t\t// of the same resource, we'll remember the most recent\n   610→\t\t\t// resource we rendered in prevResource, which is sufficient\n   611→\t\t\t// because we sorted the list of instance addresses above, and\n   612→\t\t\t// our sort order always groups together instances of the same\n   613→\t\t\t// resource.\n   614→\t\t\tresourceAddr := instAddr.ContainingResource()\n   615→\t\t\tif resourceAddr.Equal(prevResourceAddr) {\n   616→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   617→\t\t\t}\n   618→\t\t\tfmt.Fprintf(&listBuf, \"\\n  -target=%q\", resourceAddr.String())\n   619→\t\t\tprevResourceAddr = resourceAddr\n   620→\t\t}\n   621→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n   622→\t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n   623→\t\t\t\"Moved resource instances excluded by targeting\",\n   624→\t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\n   625→\t\t\t\t\"Resource instances in your current state have moved to new addresses in the latest configuration. Terraform must include those resource instances while planning in order to ensure a correct result, but your -target=... options do not fully cover all of those resource instances.\\n\\nTo create a valid plan, either remove your -target=... options altogether or add the following additional target options:%s\\n\\nNote that adding these options may include further additional resource instances in your plan, in order to respect object dependencies.\",\n   626→\t\t\t\tlistBuf.String(),\n   627→\t\t\t),\n   628→\t\t))\n   629→\t}\n   630→\n   631→\treturn diags\n   632→}\n   633→\n   634→func (c *Context) postPlanValidateMoves(config *configs.Config, stmts []refactoring.MoveStatement, allInsts instances.Set) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n   635→\treturn refactoring.ValidateMoves(stmts, config, allInsts)\n   636→}\n   637→\n   638→// findImportTargets builds a list of import targets from any import blocks in\n   639→// config.\n   640→func (c *Context) findImportTargets(config *configs.Config) []*ImportTarget {\n   641→\tvar importTargets []*ImportTarget\n   642→\tfor _, ic := range config.Module.Import {\n   643→\t\timportTargets = append(importTargets, &ImportTarget{\n   644→\t\t\tConfig: ic,\n   645→\t\t})\n   646→\t}\n   647→\treturn importTargets\n   648→}\n   649→\n   650→// findForgetTargets builds a list of resources and a list of modules to be\n   651→// forgotten, based on any removed blocks in config.\n   652→func (c *Context) findForgetTargets(config *configs.Config) (forgetResources []addrs.ConfigResource, forgetModules []addrs.Module, diags tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   653→\tremoveStmts, diags := refactoring.FindRemoveStatements(config)\n   654→\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n   655→\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n   656→\t}\n   657→\tfor _, rst := range removeStmts.Values() {\n   658→\t\tif rst.Destroy {\n   659→\t\t\t// no-op\n   660→\t\t} else {\n   661→\t\t\tif fr, ok := rst.From.(addrs.ConfigResource); ok {\n   662→\t\t\t\tforgetResources = append(forgetResources, fr)\n   663→\t\t\t} else if fm, ok := rst.From.(addrs.Module); ok {\n   664→\t\t\t\tforgetModules = append(forgetModules, fm)\n   665→\t\t\t} else {\n   666→\t\t\t\tpanic(\"Invalid ConfigMoveable type in remove statement\")\n   667→\t\t\t}\n   668→\t\t}\n   669→\t}\n   670→\treturn forgetResources, forgetModules, diags\n   671→}\n   672→\n   673→func (c *Context) planWalk(config *configs.Config, prevRunState *states.State, opts *PlanOpts) (*plans.Plan, *lang.Scope, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   674→\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n   675→\tlog.Printf(\"[DEBUG] Building and walking plan graph for %s\", opts.Mode)\n   676→\n   677→\tprevRunState = prevRunState.DeepCopy() // don't modify the caller's object when we process the moves\n   678→\tmoveStmts, moveResults, moveDiags := c.prePlanFindAndApplyMoves(config, prevRunState)\n   679→\tdiags = diags.Append(moveDiags)\n   680→\tif moveDiags.HasErrors() {\n   681→\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n   682→\t}\n   683→\n   684→\t// If resource targeting is in effect then it might conflict with the\n   685→\t// move result.\n   686→\tdiags = diags.Append(c.prePlanVerifyTargetedMoves(moveResults, opts.Targets))\n   687→\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n   688→\t\t// We'll return early here, because if we have any moved resource\n   689→\t\t// instances excluded by targeting then planning is likely to encounter\n   690→\t\t// strange problems that may lead to confusing error messages.\n   691→\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n   692→\t}\n   693→\n   694→\tgraph, walkOp, moreDiags := c.planGraph(config, prevRunState, opts)\n   695→\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n   696→\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n   697→\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n   698→\t}\n   699→\n   700→\ttimestamp := time.Now().UTC()\n   701→\tif opts.ForcePlanTimestamp != nil {\n   702→\t\t// Some tests use this to produce stable results to assert against.\n   703→\t\ttimestamp = *opts.ForcePlanTimestamp\n   704→\t}\n   705→\n   706→\tvar externalProviderConfigs map[addrs.RootProviderConfig]providers.Interface\n   707→\tif opts != nil {\n   708→\t\texternalProviderConfigs = opts.ExternalProviders\n   709→\t}\n   710→\n   711→\t// If we get here then we should definitely have a non-nil \"graph\", which\n   712→\t// we can now walk.\n   713→\tchanges := plans.NewChanges()\n   714→\n   715→\t// Initialize the results table to validate provider function calls.\n   716→\t// Hold reference to this so we can store the table data in the plan file.\n   717→\tproviderFuncResults := providers.NewFunctionResultsTable(nil)\n   718→\n   719→\twalker, walkDiags := c.walk(graph, walkOp, &graphWalkOpts{\n   720→\t\tConfig:                     config,\n   721→\t\tInputState:                 prevRunState,\n   722→\t\tExternalProviderConfigs:    externalProviderConfigs,\n   723→\t\tDeferralAllowed:            opts.DeferralAllowed,\n   724→\t\tExternalDependencyDeferred: opts.ExternalDependencyDeferred,\n   725→\t\tChanges:                    changes,\n   726→\t\tMoveResults:                moveResults,\n   727→\t\tOverrides:                  opts.Overrides,\n   728→\t\tPlanTimeTimestamp:          timestamp,\n   729→\t\tProviderFuncResults:        providerFuncResults,\n   730→\t\tForget:                     opts.Forget,\n   731→\t})\n   732→\tdiags = diags.Append(walker.NonFatalDiagnostics)\n   733→\tdiags = diags.Append(walkDiags)\n   734→\n   735→\tallInsts := walker.InstanceExpander.AllInstances()\n   736→\n   737→\tmoveValidateDiags := c.postPlanValidateMoves(config, moveStmts, allInsts)\n   738→\tif moveValidateDiags.HasErrors() {\n   739→\t\t// If any of the move statements are invalid then those errors take\n   740→\t\t// precedence over any other errors because an incomplete move graph\n   741→\t\t// is quite likely to be the _cause_ of various errors. This oddity\n   742→\t\t// comes from the fact that we need to apply the moves before we\n   743→\t\t// actually validate them, because validation depends on the result\n   744→\t\t// of first trying to plan.\n   745→\t\treturn nil, nil, moveValidateDiags\n   746→\t}\n   747→\tdiags = diags.Append(moveValidateDiags) // might just contain warnings\n   748→\n   749→\tif moveResults.Blocked.Len() > 0 && !diags.HasErrors() {\n   750→\t\t// If we had blocked moves and we're not going to be returning errors\n   751→\t\t// then we'll report the blockers as a warning. We do this only in the\n   752→\t\t// absense of errors because invalid move statements might well be\n   753→\t\t// the root cause of the blockers, and so better to give an actionable\n   754→\t\t// error message than a less-actionable warning.\n   755→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(blockedMovesWarningDiag(moveResults))\n   756→\t}\n   757→\n   758→\t// If we reach this point with error diagnostics then \"changes\" is a\n   759→\t// representation of the subset of changes we were able to plan before\n   760→\t// we encountered errors, which we'll return as part of a non-nil plan\n   761→\t// so that e.g. the UI can show what was planned so far in case that extra\n   762→\t// context helps the user to understand the error messages we're returning.\n   763→\tprevRunState = walker.PrevRunState.Close()\n   764→\n   765→\t// The refreshed state may have data resource objects which were deferred\n   766→\t// to apply and cannot be serialized.\n   767→\twalker.RefreshState.RemovePlannedResourceInstanceObjects()\n   768→\tpriorState := walker.RefreshState.Close()\n   769→\n   770→\tdriftedResources, driftDiags := c.driftedResources(config, prevRunState, priorState, moveResults)\n   771→\tdiags = diags.Append(driftDiags)\n   772→\n   773→\tdeferredResources, deferredDiags := c.deferredResources(config, walker.Deferrals.GetDeferredChanges(), priorState)\n   774→\tdiags = diags.Append(deferredDiags)\n   775→\n   776→\tvar forgottenResources []string\n   777→\tfor _, rc := range changes.Resources {\n   778→\t\tif rc.Action == plans.Forget {\n   779→\t\t\t// TODO KEM display resource ids\n   780→\t\t\tforgottenResources = append(forgottenResources, fmt.Sprintf(\" - %s\", rc.Addr))\n   781→\t\t}\n   782→\t}\n   783→\tif len(forgottenResources) > 0 {\n   784→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n   785→\t\t\ttfdiags.Warning,\n   786→\t\t\t\"Some objects will no longer be managed by Terraform\",\n   787→\t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\"If you apply this plan, Terraform will discard its tracking information for the following objects, but it will not delete them:\\n%s\\n\\nAfter applying this plan, Terraform will no longer manage these objects. You will need to import them into Terraform to manage them again.\", strings.Join(forgottenResources, \"\\n\")),\n   788→\t\t))\n   789→\t}\n   790→\tschemas, schemaDiags := c.Schemas(config, prevRunState)\n   791→\t// We must finish building a plan object, and cannot return early here.\n   792→\tvar changesSrc *plans.ChangesSrc\n   793→\tvar err error\n   794→\tif !schemaDiags.HasErrors() {\n   795→\t\tchangesSrc, err = changes.Encode(schemas)\n   796→\t\tif err != nil {\n   797→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(err)\n   798→\t\t}\n   799→\t}\n   800→\n   801→\tplan := &plans.Plan{\n   802→\t\tUIMode:                  opts.Mode,\n   803→\t\tChanges:                 changesSrc,\n   804→\t\tDriftedResources:        driftedResources,\n   805→\t\tDeferredResources:       deferredResources,\n   806→\t\tPrevRunState:            prevRunState,\n   807→\t\tPriorState:              priorState,\n   808→\t\tExternalReferences:      opts.ExternalReferences,\n   809→\t\tOverrides:               opts.Overrides,\n   810→\t\tChecks:                  states.NewCheckResults(walker.Checks),\n   811→\t\tTimestamp:               timestamp,\n   812→\t\tProviderFunctionResults: providerFuncResults.GetHashes(),\n   813→\n   814→\t\t// Other fields get populated by Context.Plan after we return\n   815→\t}\n   816→\n   817→\t// Our final rulings on whether the plan is \"complete\" and \"applyable\".\n   818→\t// See the documentation for these plan fields to learn what exactly they\n   819→\t// are intended to mean.\n   820→\tif !diags.HasErrors() {\n   821→\t\tif len(opts.Targets) == 0 && !walker.Deferrals.HaveAnyDeferrals() {\n   822→\t\t\t// A plan without any targets or deferred actions should be\n   823→\t\t\t// complete if we didn't encounter errors while producing it.\n   824→\t\t\tlog.Println(\"[TRACE] Plan is complete\")\n   825→\t\t\tplan.Complete = true\n   826→\t\t} else {\n   827→\t\t\tlog.Println(\"[TRACE] Plan is incomplete\")\n   828→\t\t}\n   829→\t\tif opts.Mode == plans.RefreshOnlyMode {\n   830→\t\t\t// In refresh-only mode we explicitly don't expect to propose any\n   831→\t\t\t// actions, but the plan is applyable if the state was changed\n   832→\t\t\t// in an interesting way by the refresh step.\n   833→\t\t\tplan.Applyable = !plan.PriorState.ManagedResourcesEqual(plan.PrevRunState) || !plan.PriorState.RootOutputValuesEqual(plan.PrevRunState)\n   834→\t\t} else {\n   835→\t\t\t// For other planning modes a plan is applyable if its \"changes\"\n   836→\t\t\t// are not considered empty (by whatever rules the plans package\n   837→\t\t\t// uses to decide that).\n   838→\t\t\tplan.Applyable = !plan.Changes.Empty()\n   839→\t\t}\n   840→\t\tif plan.Applyable {\n   841→\t\t\tlog.Println(\"[TRACE] Plan is applyable\")\n   842→\t\t} else {\n   843→\t\t\tlog.Println(\"[TRACE] Plan is not applyable\")\n   844→\t\t}\n   845→\t} else {\n   846→\t\tlog.Println(\"[WARN] Planning encountered errors, so plan is not applyable\")\n   847→\t}\n   848→\n   849→\t// The caller also gets access to an expression evaluation scope in the\n   850→\t// root module, in case it needs to extract other information using\n   851→\t// expressions, like in \"terraform console\" or the test harness.\n   852→\tevalScope := evalScopeFromGraphWalk(walker, addrs.RootModuleInstance)\n   853→\n   854→\treturn plan, evalScope, diags\n   855→}\n   856→\n   857→func (c *Context) deferredResources(config *configs.Config, deferrals []*plans.DeferredResourceInstanceChange, state *states.State) ([]*plans.DeferredResourceInstanceChangeSrc, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   858→\tvar deferredResources []*plans.DeferredResourceInstanceChangeSrc\n   859→\n   860→\tschemas, diags := c.Schemas(config, state)\n   861→\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n   862→\t\treturn deferredResources, diags\n   863→\t}\n   864→\n   865→\tfor _, deferral := range deferrals {\n   866→\n   867→\t\tschema, _ := schemas.ResourceTypeConfig(\n   868→\t\t\tdeferral.Change.ProviderAddr.Provider,\n   869→\t\t\tdeferral.Change.Addr.Resource.Resource.Mode,\n   870→\t\t\tdeferral.Change.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type)\n   871→\n   872→\t\tty := schema.ImpliedType()\n   873→\t\tdeferralSrc, err := deferral.Encode(ty)\n   874→\t\tif err != nil {\n   875→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n   876→\t\t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n   877→\t\t\t\t\"Failed to prepare deferred resource for plan\",\n   878→\t\t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\"The deferred resource %q could not be serialized to store in the plan: %s.\", deferral.Change.Addr, err)))\n   879→\t\t\tcontinue\n   880→\t\t}\n   881→\n   882→\t\tdeferredResources = append(deferredResources, deferralSrc)\n   883→\t}\n   884→\treturn deferredResources, diags\n   885→}\n   886→\n   887→func (c *Context) planGraph(config *configs.Config, prevRunState *states.State, opts *PlanOpts) (*Graph, walkOperation, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   888→\tvar externalProviderConfigs map[addrs.RootProviderConfig]providers.Interface\n   889→\tif opts != nil {\n   890→\t\texternalProviderConfigs = opts.ExternalProviders\n   891→\t}\n   892→\n   893→\tswitch mode := opts.Mode; mode {\n   894→\tcase plans.NormalMode:\n   895→\t\t// In Normal mode we need to pay attention to import and removed blocks\n   896→\t\t// in config so their targets can be added to the graph.\n   897→\t\tforgetResources, forgetModules, diags := c.findForgetTargets(config)\n   898→\t\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n   899→\t\t\treturn nil, walkPlan, diags\n   900→\t\t}\n   901→\t\tgraph, diags := (&PlanGraphBuilder{\n   902→\t\t\tConfig:                  config,\n   903→\t\t\tState:                   prevRunState,\n   904→\t\t\tRootVariableValues:      opts.SetVariables,\n   905→\t\t\tExternalProviderConfigs: externalProviderConfigs,\n   906→\t\t\tPlugins:                 c.plugins,\n   907→\t\t\tTargets:                 opts.Targets,\n   908→\t\t\tForceReplace:            opts.ForceReplace,\n   909→\t\t\tskipRefresh:             opts.SkipRefresh,\n   910→\t\t\tpreDestroyRefresh:       opts.PreDestroyRefresh,\n   911→\t\t\tOperation:               walkPlan,\n   912→\t\t\tExternalReferences:      opts.ExternalReferences,\n   913→\t\t\tOverrides:               opts.Overrides,\n   914→\t\t\tImportTargets:           c.findImportTargets(config),\n   915→\t\t\tforgetResources:         forgetResources,\n   916→\t\t\tforgetModules:           forgetModules,\n   917→\t\t\tGenerateConfigPath:      opts.GenerateConfigPath,\n   918→\t\t}).Build(addrs.RootModuleInstance)\n   919→\t\treturn graph, walkPlan, diags\n   920→\tcase plans.RefreshOnlyMode:\n   921→\t\tgraph, diags := (&PlanGraphBuilder{\n   922→\t\t\tConfig:                  config,\n   923→\t\t\tState:                   prevRunState,\n   924→\t\t\tRootVariableValues:      opts.SetVariables,\n   925→\t\t\tExternalProviderConfigs: externalProviderConfigs,\n   926→\t\t\tPlugins:                 c.plugins,\n   927→\t\t\tTargets:                 opts.Targets,\n   928→\t\t\tskipRefresh:             opts.SkipRefresh,\n   929→\t\t\tskipPlanChanges:         true, // this activates \"refresh only\" mode.\n   930→\t\t\tOperation:               walkPlan,\n   931→\t\t\tExternalReferences:      opts.ExternalReferences,\n   932→\t\t\tOverrides:               opts.Overrides,\n   933→\t\t}).Build(addrs.RootModuleInstance)\n   934→\t\treturn graph, walkPlan, diags\n   935→\tcase plans.DestroyMode:\n   936→\t\tgraph, diags := (&PlanGraphBuilder{\n   937→\t\t\tConfig:                  config,\n   938→\t\t\tState:                   prevRunState,\n   939→\t\t\tRootVariableValues:      opts.SetVariables,\n   940→\t\t\tExternalProviderConfigs: externalProviderConfigs,\n   941→\t\t\tPlugins:                 c.plugins,\n   942→\t\t\tTargets:                 opts.Targets,\n   943→\t\t\tskipRefresh:             opts.SkipRefresh,\n   944→\t\t\tOperation:               walkPlanDestroy,\n   945→\t\t\tOverrides:               opts.Overrides,\n   946→\t\t}).Build(addrs.RootModuleInstance)\n   947→\t\treturn graph, walkPlanDestroy, diags\n   948→\tdefault:\n   949→\t\t// The above should cover all plans.Mode values\n   950→\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"unsupported plan mode %s\", mode))\n   951→\t}\n   952→}\n   953→\n   954→// driftedResources is a best-effort attempt to compare the current and prior\n   955→// state. If we cannot decode the prior state for some reason, this should only\n   956→// return warnings to help the user correlate any missing resources in the\n   957→// report. This is known to happen when targeting a subset of resources,\n   958→// because the excluded instances will have been removed from the plan and\n   959→// not upgraded.\n   960→func (c *Context) driftedResources(config *configs.Config, oldState, newState *states.State, moves refactoring.MoveResults) ([]*plans.ResourceInstanceChangeSrc, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   961→\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n   962→\n   963→\tif newState.ManagedResourcesEqual(oldState) && moves.Changes.Len() == 0 {\n   964→\t\t// Nothing to do, because we only detect and report drift for managed\n   965→\t\t// resource instances.\n   966→\t\treturn nil, diags\n   967→\t}\n   968→\n   969→\tschemas, schemaDiags := c.Schemas(config, newState)\n   970→\tdiags = diags.Append(schemaDiags)\n   971→\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n   972→\t\treturn nil, diags\n   973→\t}\n   974→\n   975→\tvar drs []*plans.ResourceInstanceChangeSrc\n   976→\n   977→\tfor _, ms := range oldState.Modules {\n   978→\t\tfor _, rs := range ms.Resources {\n   979→\t\t\tif rs.Addr.Resource.Mode != addrs.ManagedResourceMode {\n   980→\t\t\t\t// Drift reporting is only for managed resources\n   981→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   982→\t\t\t}\n   983→\n   984→\t\t\tprovider := rs.ProviderConfig.Provider\n   985→\t\t\tfor key, oldIS := range rs.Instances {\n   986→\t\t\t\tif oldIS.Current == nil {\n   987→\t\t\t\t\t// Not interested in instances that only have deposed objects\n   988→\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   989→\t\t\t\t}\n   990→\t\t\t\taddr := rs.Addr.Instance(key)\n   991→\n   992→\t\t\t\t// Previous run address defaults to the current address, but\n   993→\t\t\t\t// can differ if the resource moved before refreshing\n   994→\t\t\t\tprevRunAddr := addr\n   995→\t\t\t\tif move, ok := moves.Changes.GetOk(addr); ok {\n   996→\t\t\t\t\tprevRunAddr = move.From\n   997→\t\t\t\t}\n   998→\n   999→\t\t\t\tnewIS := newState.ResourceInstance(addr)\n  1000→\n  1001→\t\t\t\tschema, _ := schemas.ResourceTypeConfig(\n  1002→\t\t\t\t\tprovider,\n  1003→\t\t\t\t\taddr.Resource.Resource.Mode,\n  1004→\t\t\t\t\taddr.Resource.Resource.Type,\n  1005→\t\t\t\t)\n  1006→\t\t\t\tif schema == nil {\n  1007→\t\t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n  1008→\t\t\t\t\t\ttfdiags.Warning,\n  1009→\t\t\t\t\t\t\"Missing resource schema from provider\",\n  1010→\t\t\t\t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\"No resource schema found for %s when decoding prior state\", addr.Resource.Resource.Type),\n  1011→\t\t\t\t\t))\n  1012→\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n  1013→\t\t\t\t}\n  1014→\t\t\t\tty := schema.ImpliedType()\n  1015→\n  1016→\t\t\t\toldObj, err := oldIS.Current.Decode(ty)\n  1017→\t\t\t\tif err != nil {\n  1018→\t\t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n  1019→\t\t\t\t\t\ttfdiags.Warning,\n  1020→\t\t\t\t\t\t\"Failed to decode resource from state\",\n  1021→\t\t\t\t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\"Error decoding %q from prior state: %s\", addr.String(), err),\n  1022→\t\t\t\t\t))\n  1023→\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n  1024→\t\t\t\t}\n  1025→\n  1026→\t\t\t\tvar newObj *states.ResourceInstanceObject\n  1027→\t\t\t\tif newIS != nil && newIS.Current != nil {\n  1028→\t\t\t\t\tnewObj, err = newIS.Current.Decode(ty)\n  1029→\t\t\t\t\tif err != nil {\n  1030→\t\t\t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n  1031→\t\t\t\t\t\t\ttfdiags.Warning,\n  1032→\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\"Failed to decode resource from state\",\n  1033→\t\t\t\t\t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\"Error decoding %q from prior state: %s\", addr.String(), err),\n  1034→\t\t\t\t\t\t))\n  1035→\t\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n  1036→\t\t\t\t\t}\n  1037→\t\t\t\t}\n  1038→\n **File**: `internal/providers/provider.go`\n   - **Request Fields**:\n     - `TypeName`: Resource type (e.g., \"aws_instance\")\n     - `Config`: HCL-evaluated configuration (marked values preserved)\n     - `PriorState`: Current state before change (null for creates)\n     - `ProposedNewState`: Theoretical new state from config\n     - `PriorPrivate`: Provider-managed sensitive data from prior state\n     - `ProviderMeta`: terraform_data values if present\n     - `ClientCapabilities.DeferralAllowed`: If deferrals permitted\n   - **Response Processing**:\n     - `resp.PlannedState`: Provider's computed new state (line 954)\n     - `resp.PlannedPrivate`: Provider's sensitive data for new state (line 955)\n     - `resp.Deferred`: Optional deferral directive (line 951)\n     - `resp.Diagnostics`: Provider warnings/errors\n\n6. **Action Determination** (lines 1042-1150, not shown in excerpt but referenced)\n   - Provider's response implicitly determines action:\n     - **Create** (`plans.Create`): `PriorState` is null, `PlannedState` is non-null\n     - **Update** (`plans.Update`): Both prior and planned differ with same values for unchanged attributes\n     - **Replace** (`plans.Replace`): Fields marked with `RequiresReplace` in schema are changed\n     - **Delete** (`plans.Delete`): Only computed during destroy plans (not here)\n     - **NoOp** (`plans.NoOp`): Prior and planned states are identical\n\n7. **Force-Replace Override** (lines 388-395 in managedResourceExecute)\n   - This resource also deferred (line 475)\n\n9. **Change Persistence** (lines 424-431 in managedResourceExecute)\n   - Write computed change to plan via `n.writeChange(ctx, change, \"\")` (line 424)\n   - Write resulting state via `n.writeResourceInstanceState(ctx, instancePlanState, workingState)` (line 428)\n\n### Refresh vs Plan Comparison\n\n**Refresh** (`n.refresh()` - line 298):\n- Calls provider's `ReadResource` RPC with current state ID\n- Returns actual remote resource attributes\n- Detects out-of-band changes and deletions\n- State is updated to reflect upstream reality\n\n**Plan** (`n.plan()` - lines 354-356):\n- Compares refreshed state (prior) with desired configuration\n- Calls provider's `PlanResourceChange` RPC\n- Provider determines if attributes require replacement or can be updated in-place\n- Produces ResourceInstanceChange with proposed action and new value\n\n### Summary: Action Determination Logic\n\nThe provider's `PlanResourceChange` determines the action by:\n1. Analyzing which configuration attributes changed from prior state\n2. For changed attributes, checking schema's `RequiresReplace` directive\n3. Returning PlannedState with sensitive fields computed\n4. Terraform Core calculates action based on schema-governed requirements\n\nThe complete resource change is captured in `plans.ResourceInstanceChange`:\n- `Addr`: Resource address\n- `ProviderAddr`: Provider configuration used\n- `Change.Action`: Create/Update/Replace/Delete/NoOp\n- `Change.Before`: Prior state value\n- `Change.After`: Planned new value\n- `Change.Importing`: If this is an import operation\n- `ActionReason`: Why action was chosen (e.g., RequiresReplace, ForcedReplace, TriggeredBy)\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Key File Paths and Line References\n\n**Command Layer**:\n- `internal/command/plan.go:22-118` - Allows provider to reject invalid config before planning\n\n4. **ignore_changes Processing** (lines 884-888)\n   - Applies `ignore_changes` attribute to preserve certain fields\n   - Must occur before PlanResourceChange for consistency\n\n5. **PlanResourceChange RPC Call** (lines 927-937)\n   ```go\n   resp = provider.PlanResourceChange(providers.PlanResourceChangeRequest{\n       TypeName:         n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type,\n       Config:           unmarkedConfigVal,\n       PriorState:       unmarkedPriorVal,\n       ProposedNewState: proposedNewVal,\n       PriorPrivate:     priorPrivate,\n       ProviderMeta:     metaConfigVal,\n       ClientCapabilities: providers.ClientCapabilities{\n           DeferralAllowed: deferralAllowed,\n       },\n   })\n   ```\n   - **File**: `internal/providers/provider.go`\n   - **Request Fields**:\n     - `TypeName`: Resource type (e.g., \"aws_instance\")\n     - `Config`: HCL-evaluated configuration (marked values preserved)\n     - `PriorState`: Current state before change (null for creates)\n     - `ProposedNewState`: Theoretical new state from config\n     - `PriorPrivate`: Provider-managed sensitive data from prior state\n     - `ProviderMeta`: terraform_data values if present\n     - `ClientCapabilities.DeferralAllowed`: If deferrals permitted\n   - **Response Processing**:\n     - `resp.PlannedState`: Provider's computed new state (line 954)\n     - `resp.PlannedPrivate`: Provider's sensitive data for new state (line 955)\n     - `resp.Deferred`: Optional deferral directive (line 951)\n     - `resp.Diagnostics`: Provider warnings/errors\n\n6. **Action Determination** (lines 1042-1150, not shown in excerpt but referenced)\n   - Provider's response implicitly determines action:\n     - **Create** (`plans.Create`): `PriorState` is null, `PlannedState` is non-null\n     - **Update** (`plans.Update`): Both prior and planned differ with same values for unchanged attributes\n     - **Replace** (`plans.Replace`): Fields marked with `RequiresReplace` in schema are changed\n     - **Delete** (`plans.Delete`): Only computed during destroy plans (not here)\n     - **NoOp** (`plans.NoOp`): Prior and planned states are identical\n\n7. **Force-Replace Override** (lines 388-395 in managedResourceExecute)\n   - If resource addr in `n.forceReplace`:\n     - Planned action is upgraded to Replace if it was NoOp or Update\n     - Change.ActionReason set to `plans.ResourceInstanceReplaceByTriggers` (line 394)\n\n8. **Deferred Actions** (lines 397-476 in managedResourceExecute)\n   - If provider returned `resp.Deferred`:\n     - Change stored in deferrals tracker (line 402)\n     - Not added to plan yet; will be revisited after dependencies resolve\n   - If dependent resource was deferred:\n     - This resource also deferred (line 475)\n\n9. **Change Persistence** (lines 424-431 in managedResourceExecute)\n   - Write computed change to plan via `n.writeChange(ctx, change, \"\")` (line 424)\n   - Write resulting state via `n.writeResourceInstanceState(ctx, instancePlanState, workingState)` (line 428)\n\n### Refresh vs Plan Comparison\n\n**Refresh** (`n.refresh()` - line 298):\n- Calls provider's `ReadResource` RPC with current state ID\n- Returns actual remote resource attributes\n- Detects out-of-band changes and deletions\n- State is updated to reflect upstream reality\n\n**Plan** (`n.plan()` - lines 354-356):\n- Compares refreshed state (prior) with desired configuration\n- Calls provider's `PlanResourceChange` RPC\n- Provider determines if attributes require replacement or can be updated in-place\n- Produces ResourceInstanceChange with proposed action and new value\n\n### Summary: Action Determination Logic\n\nThe provider's `PlanResourceChange` determines the action by:\n1. Analyzing which configuration attributes changed from prior state\n2. For changed attributes, checking schema's `RequiresReplace` directive\n3. Returning PlannedState with sensitive fields computed\n4. Terraform Core calculates action based on schema-governed requirements\n\nThe complete resource change is captured in `plans.ResourceInstanceChange`:\n- `Addr`: Resource address\n- `ProviderAddr`: Provider configuration used\n- `Change.Action`: Create/Update/Replace/Delete/NoOp\n- `Change.Before`: Prior state value\n- `Change.After`: Planned new value\n- `Change.Importing`: If this is an import operation\n- `ActionReason`: Why action was chosen (e.g., RequiresReplace, ForcedReplace, TriggeredBy)\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Key File Paths and Line References\n\n**Command Layer**:\n- `internal/command/plan.go:22-118` -
